98→  }\n    99→\n   100→  // Count severity from dimension scores\n   101→  const summary = { errors: 0, warnings: 0, info: 0 };\n   102→  if (result.dimensionScores) {\n   103→    for (const dim of 147→  if (!entries || entries.length < 2) return null;\n   148→\n   149→  const values = entries.slice(-5).map((e) => e.score);\n   150→  if (values.length < 2) return null;\n   151→\n   152→  const Before (v1)                                                                                   | After (v2)                                                                                                    |\n    49→| ------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n    50→| Source of truth    | Markdown (`AI_REVIEW_LEARNINGS_LOG.md`)                                                       | JSONL files with Zod validation                                                                               |\n    51→| Write flow         | AI writes markdown, `sync-reviews-to-jsonl.js` tries to parse it                              | AI writes structured JSONL directly via CLI writers                                                           |\n    52→| Data loss          | 85–100% field loss across key fields (pr: 76% null, patterns: 85% empty, severity: 100% zero) | 0% — Zod rejects invalid records at write time                                                                |\n    53→| Files              | 1 monolithic `reviews.jsonl` (45 entries, most fields zero)                                   | 5 split files: `reviews.jsonl`, `retros.jsonl`, `deferred-items.jsonl`, `invocations.jsonl`, `warnings.jsonl` |\n    54→| Schema enforcement | None — anything gets written                                                                  | Zod schemas defined for all 5 types (STOR-01) with write-time validation                                      |\n    55→| Queryability       | Poor — all record types in one file                                                           | Each file has independent schema, can be queried/filtered separately                                          |\n    56→\n    57→**What it solves:** The v1 JSONL layer was \"effectively non-functional as a data\n    58→store\" (S0 finding #1 from the diagnosis). The `sync-reviews-to-jsonl.js` script\n    59→destroyed 85–100% of data when parsing markdown to JSONL. All downstream\n    60→analytics, promotion, and effectiveness tracking used broken data.\n    61→\n    62→### 1.2 Completeness Model\n    63→\n    64→| Aspect                 | Before                                            | After                                                                   |\n    65→| ---------------------- | ------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n    66→| Data quality tracking  | None — records were either present or absent      | Three-tier model: `full`, `partial`, `stub` (STOR-04)                   |\n    67→| Missing field handling | Silent nulls                                      | `completeness_missing[]` array explicitly lists which fields lack data  |\n    68→| Consumer behavior      | Consumers can't distinguish \"zero\" from \"unknown\" | `hasField()` helper checks both null AND completeness_missing (STOR-08) |\n    69→\n    70→**What it solves:** Historical review data varies wildly in quality. Early\n    71→archives (reviews #1–100) are summary-only with minimal fields. The completeness\n    72→model lets consumers make informed decisions about data quality without\n    73→guessing.\n    74→\n    75→### 1.3 Origin Tracking\n    76→\n    77→| Aspect                | Before                                                                        | After                                                                               |\n    78→| --------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n    79→| Source identification | String field (`\"manual\"`, `\"session-start\"`) — 88% attributed to wrong source | Zod-validated structured object with `type`, `pr`, `round`, `tool` fields (STOR-05) |\n    80→| Source drift          | Common — \"SonarCloud + Qodo + Gemini\" collapsed to \"manual\"                   | Impossible — schema rejects malformed origin objects                                |\n    81→\n    82→### 1.4 Write Utilities\n    83→\n    84→| Aspect          | Before                                         | After                                                                                      |\n    85→| --------------- | ---------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |\n    86→| Write mechanism | Direct `fs.appendFileSync` in multiple scripts | Single shared `write-jsonl.ts` utility validates via Zod then appends (STOR-07)            |\n    87→| Read mechanism  | Raw `fs.readFileSync` + JSON.parse per-line    | `read-jsonl.ts` with schema validation and warning logging for malformed records (STOR-06) |\n    88→\n    89→**Files created:** `scripts/reviews/lib/schemas/` (6 schema files),\n    90→`scripts/reviews/lib/write-jsonl.ts`, `scripts/reviews/lib/read-jsonl.ts`,\n    91→`scripts/reviews/lib/completeness.ts`\n    92→\n    93→---\n    94→\n    95→## 2. State is stored in TWO single-source-of-truth files:\n- `.claude/state/consolidation.json` (last consolidated review, number, date)\n- `.claude/state/reviews.jsonl` (one JSON line per review entry)\n\n**Data Format:**\n\n✅ **FULLY v2 JSONL-BASED** (not v1 markdown-based):\n\n```\nLine 5: * run-consolidation.js (v2 — JSONL-based)\nLines 9-11: State lives in TWO files:\n  - .claude/state/consolidation.json\n  - .claude/state/reviews.jsonl (one JSON line per review entry)\nLine 13: NO markdown parsing for state.
